I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
oxlint(lsp): Auto-fix for unused eslint-disable directives should delete the line, not leave blank comments
### Confirm that this is a Bug for the editor extension, not the CLI

- [x] This bug does not happen in the Oxlint/Oxfmt CLI
- [x] After restarting the editor, the bug still appears

<!-- If you are able to see the same problem in the CLI, please report your issue at https://github.com/oxc-project/oxc -->

### Versions used

<!-- Please fill out the versions, hover over the Status Bar "oxc" in the bottom right to get the information as needed. -->

```
VS Code extension: v1.52.0
oxlint: v1.58.0
oxfmt: v0.43.0
VS Code version: 1.105.1
Operating System and Version: macOs 26.3.1
Node Version: v24.12.0
Node Manager: npm v11.6.2
```

### What happened?

When Oxlint reports an unused disable directive (e.g. with `reportUnusedDisableDirectives` enabled in the Oxlint config), the **CLI does not offer an auto-fix** for that diagnostic. The **VS Code extension** does apply a fix (e.g. via **Fix all** / `source.fixAll.oxc` on save), but the fix is **wrong**: it strips the directive text and leaves an **empty comment** on the line (`//` or `/**/`) instead of **removing the whole line**, which matches what users expect from ESLint-style tooling and leaves noisy, useless lines in the file.

**Steps to reproduce**
1. Clone https://github.com/arsnl/oxlint-repro-file-level-disable and open the folder in VS Code.
2. Run `npm install`.
3. In `.vscode/settings.json`, set `"source.fixAll.oxc"` to `"always"` under `editor.codeActionsOnSave` (or use **Fix all** from the lightbulb on an unused-disable diagnostic).
4. Save `test.ts` (or trigger fix all).
**Actual behavior:** Lines that contained only the disable comment become `//` or `/**/` with nothing after it.

**Expected behavior:** The **entire line** should be removed when nothing meaningful remains (same idea as removing a full `eslint-disable` line), not replaced with an empty comment token.
*(Related upstream context: in that repro, file-level `oxlint-disable` for a file-scope rule may still leave the real rule violation plus an “unused directive” warning—[that’s separate Oxlint engine behavior](https://github.com/oxc-project/oxc/issues/21072); this ticket is specifically about the **editor fix** leaving empty comments.)*

### Reproduction repo

https://github.com/arsnl/oxlint-repro-file-level-disable  

Minimal workspace: `test.ts`, `oxlint.config.ts` (`reportUnusedDisableDirectives: "warn"`), and `.vscode/` recommendations for `oxc.oxc-vscode`. See the **“Reproduction (VS Code extension)”** section in the repo `README.md`.

    11	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq)]
    12	enum DisabledRule {
    13	    /// Disables all linting rules for a span of code.
    14	    /// Used by directives like `eslint-disable`, `eslint-disable-next-line`, or `eslint-disable-line` without specific rule names.
    15	    ///
    16	    /// # Example
    17	    /// ```text
    18	    /// /* eslint-disable */
    19	    ///    ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ comment_span
    20	    /// ```
    21	    All {
    22	        /// Span of the comment containing the disable directive
    23	        comment_span: Span,
    24	        /// Whether this is a line-specific directive (`-next-line` or `-line`).
    25	        is_next_line: bool,
    26	    },
    27	    /// Disables a single specific linting rule for a span of code.
    28	    /// Used by directives like `eslint-disable rule-name`, `eslint-disable-next-line rule-name`, or `eslint-disable-line rule-name`.
    29	    ///
    30	    /// # Example
    31	    /// ```text
    32	    /// /* eslint-disable no-debugger */
    33	    ///   ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ comment_span
    34	    ///                   ^^^^^^^^^^^  name_span (for "no-debugger")
    35	    /// ```
    36	    Single {
    37	        /// Name of the disabled rule (e.g., "no-debugger", "no-console")
    38	        rule_name: String,
    39	        /// Span of the rule name within the comment.
    40	        ///
    41	        /// For `/* eslint-disable no-debugger */`, this points to "no-debugger".
    42	        name_span: Span,
    43	        /// Span of the entire comment content containing the disable directive.
    44	        ///
    45	        /// For `/* eslint-disable no-debugger */`, this points to "eslint-disable no-debugger".
    46	        comment_span: Span,
    47	        /// Whether this is a line-specific directive (`-next-line` or `-line`).
    48	        /// When true, only diagnostics starting within the interval are suppressed.
    49	        /// When false, any diagnostic overlapping the interval is suppressed.
    50	        is_next_line: bool,
    51	    },
    52	}

    55	    pub fn comment_span(&self) -> &Span {
    56	        match self {
    57	            DisabledRule::All { comment_span, .. } | DisabledRule::Single { comment_span, .. } => {
    58	                comment_span
    59	            }
    60	        }

    66	                *is_next_line
    67	            }
    68	        }

    72	/// Represents a single rule within a disable/enable comment directive.
    73	///
    74	/// Used when reporting unused disable directives or creating fixes to remove
    75	/// specific rules from a comment.
    76	///
    77	/// # Example
    78	/// ```text
    79	/// /* eslint-disable no-debugger, no-console */
    80	///                   ^^^^^^^^^^^              name_span (for this RuleCommentRule)
    81	///                   no-debugger              rule_name
    82	/// ```
    83	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq)]
    84	pub struct RuleCommentRule {
    85	    /// Name of the rule (e.g., "no-debugger", "no-console")
    86	    pub rule_name: String,
    87	    /// Span of the rule name within the comment.
    88	    ///
    89	    /// For `/* eslint-disable no-debugger, no-console */`, the first
    90	    /// `RuleCommentRule` would have a `name_span` pointing to "no-debugger".
    91	    pub name_span: Span,
    92	}
    93	
    94	impl RuleCommentRule {
    95	    #[expect(clippy::cast_possible_truncation)] // for `as u32`
    96	    pub fn create_fix(&self, source_text: &str, comment_span: Span) -> Fix {
    97	        let before_source =
    98	            &source_text[comment_span.start as usize..self.name_span.start as usize];
    99	
   100	        // check if there is a comma before the rule name
   101	        // if there is, remove the comma, whitespace and the rule name
   102	        let mut comma_before_offset = None;
   103	        for (i, c) in before_source.chars().rev().enumerate() {
   104	            if c.is_whitespace() {
   105	                continue;
   106	            }
   107	            if c == ',' {
   108	                comma_before_offset = Some(1 + i as u32);
   109	            }
   110	            break;
   111	        }
   112	
   113	        if let Some(comma_before_offset) = comma_before_offset {
   114	            return Fix::delete(Span::new(
   115	                self.name_span.start - comma_before_offset,
   116	                self.name_span.end,
   117	            ))
   118	            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion);
   119	        }
   120	
   121	        let after_source = &source_text[self.name_span.end as usize..comment_span.end as usize];
   122	
   123	        // check if there is a comma after the rule name
   124	        // if there is, remove the comma, whitespace and the rule name
   125	        let mut comma_after_offset = None;
   126	        for (i, c) in after_source.char_indices() {
   127	            if c.is_whitespace() {
   128	                continue;
   129	            }
   130	            if c == ',' {
   131	                comma_after_offset = Some(1 + i as u32);
   132	            }
   133	            break;
   134	        }
   135	
   136	        if let Some(comma_after_offset) = comma_after_offset {
   137	            return Fix::delete(Span::new(
   138	                self.name_span.start,
   139	                self.name_span.end + comma_after_offset,
   140	            ))
   141	            .with_kind(FixKind::Suggestion);
   142	        }
   143	
   144	        unreachable!(
   145	            "A `RuleCommentRule` should have a comma, because only one rule should be RuleCommentType::All"
   146	        );
   147	    }
   148	}

   151	pub enum RuleCommentType {

   153	    All,
   154	    // disable/enable only a handful of rules

   167	#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
   168	pub struct DisableDirectives {
   169	    /// All the disabled rules with their corresponding covering spans
   170	    intervals: Lapper<u32, DisabledRule>,
   171	    /// All comments that disable one or more specific rules
   172	    disable_rule_comments: Box<[DisableRuleComment]>,
   173	    /// Spans of unused enable directives
   174	    unused_enable_comments: Box<[(Option<String>, Span)]>,
   175	    /// Spans of used enable directives, to filter out unused
   176	    used_disable_comments: RefCell<Vec<DisabledRule>>,
   177	}
   178	
   179	impl DisableDirectives {
   180	    fn mark_disable_directive_used(&self, disable_directive: DisabledRule) {
   181	        self.used_disable_comments.borrow_mut().push(disable_directive);
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    pub fn contains(&self, rule_name: &str, span: Span) -> bool {
   185	        // For `eslint-disable-next-line` and `eslint-disable-line` directives, we only check
   186	        // if the diagnostic's starting position falls within the disabled interval.
   187	        // This prevents suppressing diagnostics for larger constructs (like functions) that
   188	        // contain disabled lines.
   189	        //
   190	        // For regular `eslint-disable` directives (which disable rules for the rest of the file),
   191	        // we check if any part of the diagnostic span overlaps with the disabled interval.
   192	        // This ensures that diagnostics starting before the disable comment (like no-empty-file)
   193	        // are still suppressed.
   194	        let mut has_match = false;
   195	        for interval in self.intervals.find(span.start, span.end) {
   196	            // Check if this rule should be disabled
   197	            let rule_matches = match &interval.val {
   198	                DisabledRule::All { .. } => true,
   199	                // `rule_name` does not contain the prefix.
   200	                // - `vitest/foobar` will be just `foobar`.
   201	                // - `@typescript-eslint/no-var-requires` will be just `no-var-requires`
   202	                //
   203	                // This enables matching rules across different plugins that share the same
   204	                // rule name, such as jest<->vitest rules and eslint<->typescript rules.
   205	                DisabledRule::Single { rule_name: name, .. } => {
   206	                    if name.contains(rule_name) {
   207	                        true
   208	                    } else {
   209	                        // Special-case mapping: `vitest/no-restricted-vi-methods` is implemented by `jest/no-restricted-jest-methods`.
   210	                        name == "vitest/no-restricted-vi-methods"
   211	                            && rule_name == "no-restricted-jest-methods"
   212	                    }
   213	                }
   214	            };
   215	
   216	            if !rule_matches {
   217	                continue;
   218	            }
   219	
   220	            // Check if the diagnostic span is covered by this interval
   221	            let span_covered = if interval.val.is_next_line() {
   222	                // For next-line directives, only check if the diagnostic starts within the interval
   223	                // We intentionally only check span.start (not span.end) to avoid suppressing
   224	                // diagnostics for large constructs that merely contain the disabled line
   225	                #[expect(clippy::suspicious_operation_groupings)]
   226	                {
   227	                    span.start >= interval.start && span.start < interval.stop
   228	                }
   229	            } else {
   230	                // For regular disable directives, check if there's any overlap
   231	                span.start < interval.stop && span.end > interval.start
   232	            };
   233	
   234	            if span_covered {
   235	                self.mark_disable_directive_used(interval.val.clone());
   236	                has_match = true;
   237	            }
   238	        }
   239	        has_match
   240	    }
   241	
   242	    pub fn disable_rule_comments(&self) -> &[DisableRuleComment] {
   243	        &self.disable_rule_comments
   244	    }
   245	
   246	    pub fn unused_enable_comments(&self) -> &[(Option<String>, Span)] {
   247	        &self.unused_enable_comments
   248	    }
   249	
   250	    pub fn collect_unused_disable_comments(&self) -> Vec<DisableRuleComment> {
   251	        let used = self.used_disable_comments.borrow();
   252	
   253	        self.intervals
   254	            .iter()
   255	            // 1. group intervals with the same interval.val.comment_span() together
   256	            .chunk_by(|interval| interval.val.comment_span())
   257	            .into_iter()
   258	            // 2. iterate over all groups
   259	            // 3. check if the group has only one , ore all entries with the comment span are used with `used.contains(&interval.val))`
   260	            // 4. if all entries are used, map to RuleCommentType::All comment, otherwise map to RuleCommentType::Single comment.
   261	            .filter_map(|(comment_span, group)| {
   262	                let group_vec: Vec<_> = group.collect();
   263	
   264	                if group_vec.is_empty() {
   265	                    return None;
   266	                }
   267	
   268	                let rules: Vec<RuleCommentRule> = group_vec
   269	                    .iter()
   270	                    .filter_map(|interval| {
   271	                        if used.contains(&interval.val) {
   272	                            return None;
   273	                        }
   274	                        match &interval.val {
   275	                            DisabledRule::Single { rule_name, name_span, .. } => {
   276	                                Some(RuleCommentRule {
   277	                                    rule_name: rule_name.clone(),
   278	                                    name_span: *name_span,
   279	                                })
   280	                            }
   281	                            DisabledRule::All { .. } => Some(RuleCommentRule {
   282	                                rule_name: "all".to_string(),
   283	                                name_span: *comment_span,
   284	                            }),
   285	                        }
   286	                    })
   287	                    .collect::<Vec<_>>();
   288	
   289	                if rules.is_empty() {
   290	                    return None;
   291	                }
   292	
   293	                if rules.len() == group_vec.len() {
   294	                    return Some(DisableRuleComment {
   295	                        span: *comment_span,
   296	                        r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   297	                    });
   298	                }
   299	
   300	                Some(DisableRuleComment {
   301	                    span: *comment_span,
   302	                    r#type: RuleCommentType::Single(rules),
   303	                })
   304	            })
   305	            .collect()
   306	    }
   307	}
   308	
   309	pub struct DisableDirectivesBuilder {
   310	    /// All the disabled rules with their corresponding covering spans
   311	    intervals: Lapper<u32, DisabledRule>,
   312	    /// Start of `eslint-disable` or `oxlint-disable`
   313	    disable_all_start: Option<(u32, Span)>,
   314	    /// Start of `eslint-disable` or `oxlint-disable` rule_name`
   315	    disable_start_map: FxHashMap<String, (u32, Span, Span)>,
   316	    /// All comments that disable one or more specific rules
   317	    disable_rule_comments: Vec<DisableRuleComment>,
   318	    /// Spans of unused enable directives
   319	    unused_enable_comments: Vec<(Option<String>, Span)>,
   320	}
   321	
   322	impl DisableDirectivesBuilder {
   323	    pub fn new() -> Self {
   324	        Self {
   325	            intervals: Lapper::new(vec![]),
   326	            disable_all_start: None,
   327	            disable_start_map: FxHashMap::default(),
   328	            disable_rule_comments: vec![],
   329	            unused_enable_comments: vec![],
   330	        }
   331	    }
   332	
   333	    pub fn build(mut self, source_text: &str, comments: &[Comment]) -> DisableDirectives {
   334	        self.build_impl(source_text, comments);
   335	
   336	        DisableDirectives {
   337	            intervals: self.intervals,
   338	            disable_rule_comments: self.disable_rule_comments.into_boxed_slice(),
   339	            unused_enable_comments: self.unused_enable_comments.into_boxed_slice(),
   340	            used_disable_comments: RefCell::new(Vec::new()),
   341	        }
   342	    }
   343	
   344	    fn add_interval(&mut self, start: u32, stop: u32, val: DisabledRule) {
   345	        self.intervals.insert(Interval { start, stop, val });
   346	    }
   347	
   348	    #[expect(clippy::cast_possible_truncation)] // for `as u32`
   349	    fn build_impl(&mut self, source_text: &str, comments: &[Comment]) {
   350	        let source_len = source_text.len() as u32;
   351	        // This algorithm iterates through the comments and builds all intervals
   352	        // for matching disable and enable pairs.
   353	        // Wrongly ordered matching pairs are not taken into consideration.
   354	
   355	        // NOTE: oxlint apply directive's logic not exactly same to eslint
   356	        // only `disable-all` & `enable-all`, or `disable-rule` & `enable-rule` will add to intervals for disable directives
   357	        // `disable-all` & `enable-rule` -> lone `disable-all` (enable-rule find not disable-rule before itself)
   358	        // https://github.com/eslint/eslint/blob/f67d5e875324a9d899598b11807a9c7624021432/lib/linter/apply-disable-directives.js#L308
   359	
   360	        // enable directive keep the same logic for checking unused
   361	        let mut unused_enable_directives: Vec<(Option<String>, Span)> = vec![];
   362	
   363	        for comment in comments {
   364	            let comment_span = comment.content_span();
   365	            let text_source = comment_span.source_text(source_text);
   366	            let text = text_source.trim_start();
   367	            let mut rule_name_start = comment_span.start + (text_source.len() - text.len()) as u32;
   368	
   369	            if let Some(text) =
   370	                text.strip_prefix("eslint-disable").or_else(|| text.strip_prefix("oxlint-disable"))
   371	            {
   372	                rule_name_start += 14; // eslint-disable and oxlint-disable are each 14 bytes
   373	                // `eslint-disable`
   374	                if text.trim().is_empty() {
   375	                    if self.disable_all_start.is_none() {
   376	                        self.disable_all_start = Some((comment_span.end, comment_span));
   377	                    }
   378	                    self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   379	                        span: comment_span,
   380	                        r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   381	                    });
   382	                    continue;
   383	                }
   384	                // `eslint-disable-next-line`
   385	                else if let Some(text) = text.strip_prefix("-next-line") {
   386	                    rule_name_start += 10; // -next-line is 10 bytes
   387	                    // Get the span up to the next new line
   388	                    let mut stop = comment_span.end;
   389	                    let mut lines_after_comment_end =
   390	                        source_text[comment_span.end as usize..].split_inclusive('\n');
   391	
   392	                    if let Some(rest_of_line) = lines_after_comment_end.next() {
   393	                        stop += rest_of_line.len() as u32;
   394	                    }
   395

    44	fn miette_severity_to_lsp_severity(value: Severity) -> DiagnosticSeverity {
    45	    match value {
    46	        Severity::Error => DiagnosticSeverity::ERROR,
    47	        Severity::Warning => DiagnosticSeverity::WARNING,
    48	        Severity::Advice => DiagnosticSeverity::HINT,
    49	    }

    53	#[expect(clippy::cast_possible_truncation)]
    54	pub fn message_to_lsp_diagnostic(
    55	    message: Message,
    56	    uri: &Uri,
    57	    source_text: &str,
    58	    rope: &Rope,
    59	) -> DiagnosticReport {
    60	    let severity = miette_severity_to_lsp_severity(message.error.severity);
    61	
    62	    let related_information = message.error.labels.as_ref().map(|spans| {
    63	        spans
    64	            .iter()
    65	            .map(|span| {
    66	                let offset = span.offset() as u32;
    67	                let start_position = offset_to_position(rope, offset, source_text);
    68	                let end_position =
    69	                    offset_to_position(rope, offset + span.len() as u32, source_text);
    70	
    71	                ls_types::DiagnosticRelatedInformation {

    75	                    },

    82	    });

    85	    let end_position = offset_to_position(rope, message.span.end, source_text);
    86	    let range = Range::new(start_position, end_position);

   111	    }
   112	
   113	    // 1) Use `fixed_content.message` if it exists
   114	    // 2) Try to parse the report diagnostic message
   115	    // 3) Fallback to "Fix this problem"
   116	    let alternative_fix_title: Cow<'static, str> =
   117	        if let Some(code) = message.error.message.split(':').next() {
   118	            format!("Fix this {code} problem").into()
   119	        } else {
   120	            std::borrow::Cow::Borrowed("Fix this problem")
   121	        };
   122	
   123	    let diagnostic = Diagnostic {
   124	        range,
   125	        severity: Some(severity),
   126	        code: Some(NumberOrString::String(code)),
   127	        message: diagnostic_message,
   128	        source: Some("oxc".into()),
   129	        code_description,
   130	        related_information,
   131	        tags: None,
   132	        data: None,
   133	    };
   134	
   135	    let mut fixed_content = vec![];
   136	    // Convert PossibleFixes directly to PossibleFixContent
   137	    match message.fixes {
   138	        PossibleFixes::None => {}
   139	        PossibleFixes::Single(mut fix) => {
   140	            if fix.message.is_none() {
   141	                fix.message = Some(alternative_fix_title);
   142	            }
   143	            fixed_content.push(fix_to_fixed_content(
   144	                &fix,
   145	                rope,
   146	                source_text,
   147	                FixedContentKind::LintRule,
   148	            ));
   149	        }
   150	        PossibleFixes::Multiple(fixes) => {
   151	            fixed_content.extend(fixes.into_iter().map(|mut fix| {
   152	                if fix.message.is_none() {
   153	                    fix.message = Some(alternative_fix_title.clone());
   154	                }
   155	                fix_to_fixed_content(&fix, rope, source_text, FixedContentKind::LintRule)
   156	            }));
   157	        }
   158	    }
   159	
   160	    // Add ignore fixes
   161	    let error_offset = message.span.start;
   162	    let section_offset = message.section_offset;
   163	
   164	    // If the error is exactly at the section offset and has 0 span length, it means that the file is the problem
   165	    // and attaching a ignore comment would not ignore the error.
   166	    // This is because the ignore comment would need to be placed before the error offset, which is not possible.
   167	    if error_offset == section_offset && message.span.end == section_offset {
   168	        return DiagnosticReport {
   169	            diagnostic,
   170	            code_action: Some(LinterCodeAction { range, fixed_content }),
   171	        };
   172	    }
   173	
   174	    add_ignore_fixes(
   175	        &mut fixed_content,
   176	        &message.error.code,
   177	        error_offset,
   178	        section_offset,
   179	        rope,
   180	        source_text,
   181	    );
   182	
   183	    let code_action = if fixed_content.is_empty() {
   184	        None
   185	    } else {
   186	        Some(LinterCodeAction { range, fixed_content })
   187	    };
   188	
   189	    DiagnosticReport { diagnostic, code_action }
   190	}
   191	
   192	fn fix_to_fixed_content(
   193	    fix: &Fix,
   194	    rope: &Rope,
   195	    source_text: &str,
   196	    fix_kind: FixedContentKind,
   197	) -> FixedContent {
   198	    let start_position = offset_to_position(rope, fix.span.start, source_text);
   199	    let end_position = offset_to_position(rope, fix.span.end, source_text);
   200	
   201	    debug_assert!(
   202	        fix.message.is_some(),
   203	        "Fix message should be present. `message_to_lsp_diagnostic` should modify fixes to include messages."
   204	    );
   205	
   206	    FixedContent {
   207	        message: fix.message.as_ref().map(std::string::ToString::to_string).unwrap_or_default(),
   208	        code: fix.content.to_string(),
   209	        range: Range::new(start_position, end_position),
   210	        kind: fix.kind,
   211	        lsp_kind: fix_kind,
   212	    }
   213	}
   214	
   215	pub fn generate_inverted_diagnostics(
   216	    diagnostics: &[DiagnosticReport],
   217	    uri: &Uri,
   218	) -> Vec<DiagnosticReport> {
   219	    let mut inverted_diagnostics = vec![];
   220	    for d in diagnostics {
   221	        let Some(related_info) = &d.diagnostic.related_information else {
   222	            continue;
   223	        };
   224	        let related_information = Some(vec![DiagnosticRelatedInformation {
   225	            location: ls_types::Location { uri: uri.clone(), range: d.diagnostic.range },
   226	            message: "original diagnostic".to_string(),
   227	        }]);
   228	        for r in related_info {
   229	            if r.location.range == d.diagnostic.range {
   230	                continue;
   231	            }
   232	            // If there is no message content for this span, then don't produce an additional diagnostic
   233	            // which also has no content. This prevents issues where editors expect diagnostics to have messages.
   234	            if r.message.is_empty() {
   235	                continue;
   236	            }
   237	            inverted_diagnostics.push(DiagnosticReport {
   238	                diagnostic: Diagnostic {
   239	                    range: r.location.range,
   240	                    severity: Some(DiagnosticSeverity::HINT),
   241	                    code: None,
   242	                    message: r.message.clone(),
   243	                    source: d.diagnostic.source.clone(),
   244	                    code_description: None,
   245	                    related_information: related_information.clone(),
   246	                    tags: None,
   247	                    data: None,
   248	                },
   249	                code_action: None,
   250	            });
   251	        }
   252	    }
   253	    inverted_diagnostics
   254	}
   255	
   256	/// Generate diagnostics for unused disable directives, with fixes to remove them.
   257	pub fn create_unused_directives_report(
   258	    directives: &DisableDirectives,
   259	    severity: AllowWarnDeny,
   260	    source_text: &str,
   261	    rope: &Rope,
   262	) -> Vec<DiagnosticReport> {
   263	    let mut reports = Vec::new();
   264	    let fix_message = "remove unused disable directive";
   265	
   266	    let severity = if severity == AllowWarnDeny::Deny {
   267	        DiagnosticSeverity::ERROR
   268	    } else {
   269	        DiagnosticSeverity::WARNING
   270	    };
   271	
   272	    // Report unused disable comments
   273	    let unused_disable = directives.collect_unused_disable_comments();
   274	    for unused_comment in unused_disable {
   275	        let span = unused_comment.span;
   276	        match unused_comment.r#type {
   277	            RuleCommentType::All => {
   278	                reports.push(build_unused_disable_diagnostic_report(
   279	                    "Unused oxlint-disable directive (no problems were reported).".to_string(),
   280	                    span,
   281	                    severity,
   282	                    source_text,
   283	                    rope,
   284	                    Some(&Fix::delete(span).with_message(fix_message)),
   285	                ));
   286	            }
   287	            RuleCommentType::Single(rules) => {
   288	                for rule in rules {
   289	                    reports.push(build_unused_disable_diagnostic_report(
   290	                        format!(
   291	                            "Unused oxlint-disable directive (no problems were reported from {}).",
   292	                            rule.rule_name
   293	                        ),
   294	                        rule.name_span,
   295	                        severity,
   296	                        source_text,
   297	                        rope,
   298	                        Some(&rule.create_fix(source_text, span).with_message(fix_message)),
   299	                    ));
   300	                }
   301	            }
   302	        }
   303	    }
   304	
   305	    // Report unused enable comments
   306	    let unused_enable = directives.unused_enable_comments();
   307	    for (rule_name, span) in unused_enable {
   308	        let message = if let Some(rule_name) = rule_name {
   309	            format!(
   310	                "Unused oxlint-enable directive (no matching oxlint-disable directives were found for {rule_name})."
   311	            )
   312	        } else {
   313	            "Unused oxlint-enable directive (no matching oxlint-disable directives were found)."
   314	                .to_string()
   315	        };
   316	        reports.push(build_unused_disable_diagnostic_report(
   317	            message,
   318	            *span,
   319	            severity,
   320	            source_text,
   321	            rope,
   322	            // TODO: fixer
   323	            // copy the structure of disable directives
   324	            None,
   325	        ));
   326	    }
   327	
   328	    reports
   329	}
   330	
   331	fn build_unused_disable_diagnostic_report(
   332	    message: String,
   333	    span: Span,
   334	    severity: DiagnosticSeverity,
   335	    source_text: &str,
   336	    rope: &Rope,
   337	    fix: Option<&Fix>,
   338	) -> DiagnosticReport {
   339	    let start_position = offset_to_position(rope, span.start, source_text);
   340	    let end_position = offset_to_position(rope, span.end, source_text);
   341	    let range = Range::new(start_position, end_position);
   342	
   343	    DiagnosticReport {
   344	        diagnostic: Diagnostic {
   345	            range,
   346	            severity: Some(severity),
   347	            code: Some("".into()),
   348	            message,
   349	            source: Some("oxc".into()),
   350	            code_description: None,
   351	            related_information: None,
   352	            tags: None,
   353	            data: None,
   354	        },
   355	        code_action: fix.map(|fix| LinterCodeAction {
   356	            range,
   357	            fixed_content: vec![fix_to_fixed_content(
   358	                fix,
   359	                rope,
   360	                source_text,
   361	                FixedContentKind::UnusedDirective,
   362	            )],
   363	        }),
   364	    }
   365	}
   366	
   367	pub fn offset_to_position(rope: &Rope, offset: u32, source_text: &str) -> Position {
   368	    let (line, column) = get_line_column(rope, offset, source_text);
   369	    Position::new(line, column)
   370	}
   371	
   372	/// Counter part of `oxc_linter::*::plugin_name_to_prefix`.
   373	fn prefix_to_plugin_name(prefix: &str) -> &str {
   374	    match prefix {
   375	        "eslint-plugin-import" => "import",
   376	        "eslint-plugin-jest" => "jest",
   377	        "eslint-plugin-jsdoc" => "jsdoc",
   378	        "eslint-plugin-jsx-a11y" => "jsx_a11y",
   379	        "eslint-plugin-next" => "nextjs",
   380	        "eslint-plugin-promise" => "promise",
   381	        "eslint-plugin-react-perf" => "react_perf",
   382	        "eslint-plugin-react" => "react",
   383	        "typescript-eslint" => "typescript",
   384	        "eslint-plugin-unicorn" => "unicorn",
   385	        "eslint-plugin-vitest" => "vitest",
   386	        "eslint-plugin-node" => "node",
   387	        "eslint-plugin-vue" => "vue",
   388	        _ => prefix,
   389	    }
   390	}
   391	/// Add "ignore this line" and "ignore this rule" fixes to the existing fixes.
   392	/// These fixes will be added to the end of the existing fixes.
   393	/// If the existing fixes already contain an "remove unused disable directive" fix,
   394	/// then no ignore fixes will be added.
   395	fn add_ignore_fixes(
   396	    fixes: &mut Vec<FixedContent>,
   397	    code: &OxcCode,
   398	    error_offset: u32,
   399	    section_offset: u32,
   400	    rope: &Rope,
   401	    source_text: &str,
   402	) {
   403	    debug_assert!(
   404	        !fixes.iter().any(|fix| fix.message.starts_with("remove unused disable directive")),
   405	        "Unused disable directives should never pass pass this point, as they should be handled separately in `create_unused_directives_messages`."
   406	    );
   407	
   408	    if let Some(rule_name) = code.number.as_ref() {
   409	        // this conversion is a bit messy, but basically we need to reconstruct the rule name with plugin prefix
   410	        let rule_name_with_plugin = if let Some(scope) = &code.scope
   411	            && !scope.is_empty()
   412	            // eslint does not has a plugin prefix
   413	            && scope != "eslint"
   414	        {
   415	            format!("{}/{rule_name}", prefix_to_plugin_name(scope))
   416	        } else {
   417	            rule_name.to_string()
   418	        };
   419	
   420	        // TODO: doesn't support disabling multiple rules by name for a given line.
   421	        fixes.push(disable_for_this_line(
   422	            &rule_name_with_plugin,
   423	            error_offset,
   424	            section_offset,
   425	            rope,
   426	            source_text,
   427	        ));
   428	        fixes.push(disable_for_this_section(
   429	            &rule_name_with_plugin,
   430	            section_offset,
   431	            rope,
   432	            source_text,
   433	        ));
   434	    }
   435	}
   436	
   437	fn disable_for_this_line(
   438	    rule_name: &str,
   439	    error_offset: u32,
   440	    section_offset: u32,
   441	    rope: &Rope,
   442	    source_text: &str,
   443	) -> FixedContent {
   444	    let bytes = source_text.as_bytes();
   445	    // Find the line break before the error
   446	    let mut line_break_offset = error_offset;
   447	    for byte in bytes[section_offset as usize..error_offset as usize].iter().rev() {
   448	        if *byte == b'\n' || *byte == b'\r' {
   449	            break;
   450	        }
   451	        line_break_offset -= 1;
   452	    }
   453	
   454	    // For framework files, ensure we don't go before the section start
   455	    if section_offset > 0 && line_break_offset < section_offset {
   456	        line_break_offset = section_offset;
   457	    }
   458	
   459	    let (content_prefix, insert_offset) =
   460	        get_section_insert_position(section_offset, line_break_offset, bytes);
   461	
   462	    let whitespace_range = {
   463	        let start = insert_offset as usize;
   464	        let end = error_offset as usize;
   465	
   466	        // make sure that end is at least start to avoid panic
   467	        let end = end.max(start);
   468	        let slice = &bytes[start..end];
   469	        let whitespace_len = slice.iter().take_while(|c| matches!(c, b' ' | b'\t')).count();
   470	        &slice[..whitespace_len]
   471	    };

     8	use bitflags::bitflags;

    10	use oxc_span::{GetSpan, SPAN, Span};
    11	
    12	bitflags! {
    13	    /// Flags describing an automatic code fix.
    14	    ///
    15	    /// These are used by lint rules when they provide a code fix or suggestion.
    16	    /// These are also used by the `LintService` to decide which kinds of
    17	    /// changes to apply.
    18	    ///
    19	    /// [`FixKind`] is designed to be interoperable with [`bool`]. `true` turns
    20	    /// into [`FixKind::Fix`] (applies only safe fixes) and `false` turns into
    21	    /// [`FixKind::None`] (do not apply any fixes or suggestions).
    22	    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash)]
    23	    pub struct FixKind: u8 {
    24	        /// An automatic code fix. Most of these are applied with `--fix`
    25	        ///
    26	        const Fix = 1 << 0;
    27	        /// A recommendation about how to fix a rule violation. These are usually
    28	        /// safe to apply, in that they shouldn't cause parse or runtime errors,
    29	        /// but may change the meaning of the code.
    30	        const Suggestion = 1 << 1;
    31	        /// Marks a fix or suggestion as dangerous. Dangerous fixes/suggestions
    32	        /// may break the code. Covers cases that are
    33	        /// - Aggressive (e.g. some code removal)
    34	        /// - Are under development. Think of this as similar to the `nursery`
    35	        ///   rule category.
    36	        const Dangerous = 1 << 2;
    37	
    38	        const SafeFix = Self::Fix.bits();
    39	        const SafeFixOrSuggestion = Self::Fix.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    40	        const DangerousFix = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Fix.bits();
    41	        const DangerousSuggestion = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    42	        const DangerousFixOrSuggestion = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Fix.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    43	
    44	        /// Used to specify that no fixes should be applied.
    45	        const None = 0;
    46	        /// Fixes and Suggestions that are safe or dangerous.
    47	        const All = Self::Dangerous.bits() | Self::Fix.bits() | Self::Suggestion.bits();
    48	    }
    49	}
    50	
    51	// explicit definition for clarity
    52	impl Default for FixKind {
    53	    #[inline]
    54	    fn default() -> Self {
    55	        Self::None
    56	    }
    57	}
    58	
    59	impl FixKind {
    60	    #[inline]
    61	    pub const fn is_none(self) -> bool {
    62	        self.is_empty()
    63	    }
    64	
    65	    #[inline]
    66	    pub const fn is_some(self) -> bool {
    67	        self.bits() > 0
    68	    }
    69	
    70	    #[inline]
    71	    pub const fn is_dangerous(self) -> bool {
    72	        self.contains(Self::Dangerous)
    73	    }
    74	
    75	    /// Check if a fix produced by a lint rule is allowed to be applied
    76	    /// to the source code.
    77	    ///
    78	    /// Here, `self` is the set of allowed [`FixKind`]s, and `rule_fix` is the
    79	    /// kind of fixed produced by the rule.
    80	    ///
    81	    /// # Example
    82	    /// ```
    83	    /// use oxc_linter::FixKind;
    84	    ///
    85	    /// // `none` means no fixes will be applied at all
    86	    /// assert!(!FixKind::None.can_apply(FixKind::SafeFix));
    87	    ///
    88	    /// // allow safe fixes
    89	    /// assert!(FixKind::SafeFix.can_apply(FixKind::SafeFix));
    90	    /// assert!(!FixKind::SafeFix.can_apply(FixKind::DangerousFix)); // not safe
    91	    /// assert!(!FixKind::SafeFix.can_apply(FixKind::Suggestion));   // not a fix
    92	    /// ```
    93	    #[inline]
    94	    pub fn can_apply(self, rule_fix: Self) -> bool {
    95	        self.contains(rule_fix)
    96	    }
    97	
    98	    /// # Panics
    99	    /// If this [`FixKind`] is only [`FixKind::Dangerous`] without a
   100	    /// [`FixKind::Fix`] or [`FixKind::Suggestion`] qualifier.
   101	    pub fn emoji(self) -> &'static str {
   102	        if self.is_empty() {
   103	            return "";
   104	        }
   105	        match self {
   106	            Self::Fix => "🛠️",
   107	            Self::Suggestion => "💡",
   108	            Self::SafeFixOrSuggestion => "🛠️💡",
   109	            Self::DangerousFixOrSuggestion => "⚠️🛠️️💡",
   110	            Self::DangerousFix => "⚠️🛠️️",
   111	            Self::DangerousSuggestion => "⚠️💡",
   112	            Self::Dangerous => panic!(
   113	                "Fix kinds cannot just be dangerous, they must also be 'Fix' or 'Suggestion'."
   114	            ),
   115	            _ => {
   116	                debug_assert!(false, "Please add an emoji for FixKind: {self:?}");
   117	                ""
   118	            }
   119	        }
   120	    }
   121	
   122	    /// Returns a string representation of the fix kind.
   123	    ///
   124	    /// This method returns a lowercase, underscore-separated string
   125	    /// representing all possible fix kind combinations.
   126	    pub fn to_string(self) -> &'static str {
   127	        if self.is_empty() {
   128	            return "none";
   129	        }
   130	        match self {
   131	            Self::Fix => "fix",
   132	            Self::Suggestion => "suggestion",
   133	            Self::Dangerous => "dangerous",
   134	            Self::SafeFixOrSuggestion => "safe_fix_or_suggestion",
   135	            Self::DangerousFix => "dangerous_fix",
   136	            Self::DangerousSuggestion => "dangerous_suggestion",
   137	            Self::DangerousFixOrSuggestion => "dangerous_fix_or_suggestion",
   138	            _ => {
   139	                debug_assert!(false, "Unhandled FixKind combination: {self:?}");
   140	                "unknown"
   141	            }
   142	        }
   143	    }
   144	}
   145	
   146	// TODO: rename
   147	#[derive(Debug, Default)]
   148	#[must_use = "Fixes must be used. If you don't need a fix, use `LintContext::diagnostic`, or create an empty fix using `RuleFixer::noop`."]
   149	pub struct RuleFix {
   150	    kind: FixKind,
   151	    /// A suggestion message. Will be shown in editors via code actions.
   152	    message: Option<Cow<'static, str>>,
   153	    /// The actual fix that will be applied to the source code.
   154	    ///
   155	    /// See: [`Fix`]
   156	    fix: CompositeFix,
   157	}

   159	macro_rules! impl_from {
   160	    ($($ty:ty),*) => {
   161	        $(
   162	            impl From<$ty> for RuleFix {
   163	                fn from(fix: $ty) -> Self {
   164	                    Self { kind: FixKind::SafeFix, message: None, fix: fix.into() }
   165	                }
   166	            }

   179	            message: None,
   180	            fix: iter.into_iter().collect::<Vec<_>>().into(),

   192	impl RuleFix {
   193	    #[inline]
   194	    pub(super) fn new(
   195	        kind: FixKind,
   196	        message: Option<Cow<'static, str>>,
   197	        fix: CompositeFix,
   198	    ) -> Self {
   199	        Self { kind, message, fix }
   200	    }
   201	
   202	    /// Create a new safe fix.
   203	    #[inline]
   204	    pub fn fix(fix: CompositeFix) -> Self {
   205	        Self { kind: FixKind::Fix, message: None, fix }
   206	    }
   207	
   208	    /// Create a new suggestion
   209	    #[inline]
   210	    pub const fn suggestion(fix: CompositeFix, message: Cow<'static, str>) -> Self {
   211	        Self { kind: FixKind::Suggestion, message: Some(message), fix }
   212	    }
   213	
   214	    /// Create a dangerous fix.
   215	    #[inline]
   216	    pub fn dangerous(fix: CompositeFix) -> Self {
   217	        Self { kind: FixKind::DangerousFix, message: None, fix }
   218	    }
   219	
   220	    /// Mark this [`RuleFix`] as dangerous.
   221	    ///
   222	    /// This is especially useful for fixer functions that are safe in some
   223	    /// cases but not in others.
   224	    ///
   225	    /// # Example
   226	    ///
   227	    /// ```ignore
   228	    /// use oxc_linter::fixer::{RuleFix, RuleFixer};
   229	    /// use oxc_ast::ast::Expression;
   230	    ///
   231	    /// fn my_fixer<'a>(fixer: RuleFixer<'a>, bad_node: &Expression<'a>) -> RuleFix<'a> {
   232	    ///   fixer.delete(bad_node).dangerously()
   233	    /// }
   234	    ///
   235	    /// fn is_dangerous(bad_node: &Expression<'_>) -> bool {
   236	    ///   // some check on bad_node
   237	    /// #  true
   238	    /// }
   239	    ///
   240	    /// fn maybe_dangerous_fixer<'a>(fixer: RuleFixer<'a>, bad_node: &Expression<'a>) -> RuleFix<'a> {
   241	    ///   let fix = fixer.delete(bad_node);
   242	    ///   if is_dangerous() {
   243	    ///     fix.dangerously()
   244	    ///   } else {
   245	    ///     fix
   246	    ///   }
   247	    /// }
   248	    /// ```
   249	    pub fn dangerously(mut self) -> Self {
   250	        self.kind.set(FixKind::Dangerous, true);
   251	        self
   252	    }
   253	
   254	    #[inline]
   255	    pub fn with_message<S: Into<Cow<'static, str>>>(mut self, message: S) -> Self {
   256	        self.message = Some(message.into());
   257	        self
   258	    }
   259	
   260	    #[inline]
   261	    pub fn kind(&self) -> FixKind {
   262	        self.kind
   263	    }
   264	
   265	    #[inline]
   266	    pub fn message(&self) -> Option<&str> {
   267	        self.message.as_deref()
   268	    }
   269	
   270	    #[inline]
   271	    pub fn into_fix(self, source_text: &str) -> Fix {
   272	        // If there is only one fix, use the message from that fix.
   273	        let message = match &self.fix {
   274	            CompositeFix::Single(fix) if fix.message.as_ref().is_some_and(|m| !m.is_empty()) => {
   275	                fix.message.clone()
   276	            }
   277	            _ => self.message,
   278	        };
   279	        let mut fix = self.fix.normalize_fixes(source_text);
   280	        fix.message = message;
   281	        fix.kind = self.kind;
   282	        fix
   283	    }
   284	
   285	    #[inline]
   286	    pub fn extend<F: Into<CompositeFix>>(mut self, fix: F) -> Self {
   287	        self.fix = self.fix.concat(fix.into());
   288	        self
   289	    }
   290	
   291	    #[inline]
   292	    pub fn push<F: Into<CompositeFix>>(&mut self, fix: F) {
   293	        self.fix.push(fix.into());
   294	    }
   295	}
   296	
   297	impl GetSpan for RuleFix {
   298	    fn span(&self) -> Span {
   299	        self.fix.span()
   300	    }
   301	}

   307	        &self.fix
   308	    }

   311	/// A completed, normalized fix ready to be applied to the source code.
   312	///
   313	/// Used internally by this module. Lint rules should use `RuleFix`.
   314	#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
   315	#[non_exhaustive]
   316	pub struct Fix {
   317	    pub content: Cow<'static, str>,
   318	    /// A brief suggestion message describing the fix. Will be shown in
   319	    /// editors via code actions.
   320	    pub message: Option<Cow<'static, str>>,
   321	    pub kind: FixKind,
   322	    pub span: Span,
   323	}
   324	
   325	impl Default for Fix {
   326	    fn default() -> Self {
   327	        Self::empty()
   328	    }
   329	}
   330	
   331	impl Fix {
   332	    pub const fn delete(span: Span) -> Self {
   333	        Self { content: Cow::Borrowed(""), message: None, span, kind: FixKind::None }
   334	    }
   335	
   336	    pub fn new<T: Into<Cow<'static, str>>>(content: T, span: Span) -> Self {
   337	        Self { content: content.into(), message: None, span, kind: FixKind::None }
   338	    }
   339	
   340	    /// Creates a [`Fix`] that doesn't change the source code.
   341	    #[inline]
   342	    pub const fn empty() -> Self {
   343	        Self { content: Cow::Borrowed(""), message: None, span: SPAN, kind: FixKind::None }
   344	    }
   345	
   346	    #[must_use]
   347	    pub fn with_message(mut self, message: impl Into<Cow<'static, str>>) -> Self {
   348	        self.message = Some(message.into());
   349	        self
   350	    }
   351	
   352	    #[must_use]
   353	    pub fn with_kind(mut self, kind: FixKind) -> Self {
   354	        self.kind = kind;
   355	        self
   356	    }
   357	}
   358	
   359	#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
   360	pub enum PossibleFixes {
   361	    None,
   362	    Single(Fix),
   363	    Multiple(Vec<Fix>),
   364	}
   365	
   366	impl PossibleFixes {
   367	    /// Gets the number of [`Fix`]es contained in this [`PossibleFixes`].
   368	    pub fn len(&self) -> usize {
   369	        match self {
   370	            PossibleFixes::None => 0,
   371	            PossibleFixes::Single(_) => 1,
   372	            PossibleFixes::Multiple(fixes) => fixes.len(),
   373	        }
   374	    }
   375	
   376	    /// Returns `true` if this [`PossibleFixes`] contains no [`Fix`]es
   377	    pub fn is_empty(&self) -> bool {
   378	        self.len() == 0
   379	    }
   380	
   381	    pub fn span(&self) -> Span {
   382	        match self {
   383	            PossibleFixes::None => SPAN,
   384	            PossibleFixes::Single(fix) => fix.span,
   385	            PossibleFixes::Multiple(fixes) => {
   386	                fixes.iter().map(|fix| fix.span).reduce(Span::merge).unwrap_or(SPAN)
   387	            }
   388	        }
   389	    }
   390	}
   391	
   392	impl From<Option<Fix>> for PossibleFixes {
   393	    /// Create a new [`PossibleFixes`] from an `Option<Fix>`.
   394	    fn from(fix: Option<Fix>) -> Self {
   395	        match fix {
   396	            Some(fix) => PossibleFixes::Single(fix),
   397	            None => PossibleFixes::None,
   398	        }
   399	    }
   400	}
   401	
   402	impl FromIterator<Fix> for PossibleFixes {
   403	    /// Create a new [`PossibleFixes`] from an iterator of [`Fix`]es.
   404	    fn from_iter<T: IntoIterator<Item = Fix>>(fixes: T) -> Self {
   405	        let mut fixes = fixes.into_iter();
   406	
   407	        if let Some(first_fix) = fixes.next() {
   408	            if let Some(second_fix) = fixes.next() {
   409	                PossibleFixes::Multiple(iter::chain([first_fix, second_fix], fixes).collect())
   410	            } else {
   411	                PossibleFixes::Single(first_fix)
   412	            }
   413	        } else {
   414	            PossibleFixes::None
   415	        }
   416	    }
   417	}
   418	
   419	// NOTE (@DonIsaac): having these variants is effectively the same as interning
   420	// single or 0-element Vecs. I experimented with using smallvec here, but the
   421	// resulting struct size was larger (40 bytes vs 32). So, we're sticking with
   422	// this (at least for now).
   423	#[derive(Debug, Default)]
   424	pub enum CompositeFix {
   425	    /// No fixes
   426	    #[default]
   427	    None,
   428	    Single(Fix),
   429	    /// Several fixes that will be merged into one, in order.
   430	    Multiple(Vec<Fix>),
   431	}
   432	
   433	impl From<Fix> for CompositeFix {
   434	    fn from(fix: Fix) -> Self {
   435	        CompositeFix::Single(fix)
   436	    }
   437	}
   438	
   439	impl From<Option<Fix>> for CompositeFix {
   440	    fn from(fix: Option<Fix>) -> Self {
   441	        match fix {
   442	            Some(fix) => CompositeFix::Single(fix),
   443	            None => CompositeFix::None,
   444	        }
   445	    }
   446	}
   447	
   448	impl From<Vec<Fix>> for CompositeFix {
   449	    fn from(mut fixes: Vec<Fix>) -> Self {
   450	        match fixes.len() {
   451	            0 => CompositeFix::None,
   452	            // fixes[0] doesn't correctly move the vec's entry
   453	            1 => CompositeFix::Single(fixes.pop().unwrap()),
   454	            _ => CompositeFix::Multiple(fixes),
   455	        }
   456	    }
   457	}
   458	
   459	impl From<Vec<CompositeFix>> for CompositeFix {
   460	    fn from(fixes: Vec<Self>) -> Self {
   461	        fixes.into_iter().reduce(Self::concat).unwrap_or_default()
   462	    }
   463	}
   464	
   465	impl GetSpan for CompositeFix {
   466	    fn span(&self) -> Span {
   467	        match self {
   468	            CompositeFix::Single(fix) => fix.span,
   469	            CompositeFix::Multiple(fixes) => {
   470	                fixes.iter().map(|fix| fix.span).reduce(Span::merge).unwrap_or(SPAN)
   471	            }
   472	            CompositeFix::None => SPAN,
   473	        }
   474	    }
   475	}
   476	
   477	impl CompositeFix {
   478	    pub fn push(&mut self, fix: CompositeFix) {
   479	        match self {
   480	            Self::None => *self = fix,
   481	            Self::Single(fix1) => match fix {
   482	                Self::None => {}
   483	                Self::Single(other_fix) => {
   484	                    *self = Self::Multiple(vec![std::mem::take(fix1), other_fix]);
   485	                }
   486	                Self::Multiple(mut fixes) => {
   487	                    fixes.insert(0, std::mem::take(fix1));
   488	                    *self = Self::Multiple(fixes);
   489	                }
   490	            },
   491	            Self::Multiple(fixes) => match fix {
   492	                Self::None => {}
   493	                Self::Single(fix) => {
   494	                    fixes.push(fix);
   495	                }
   496	                Self::Multiple(other_fixes) => fixes.extend(other_fixes),
   497	            },
   498	        }
   499	    }
   500	
   501	    #[cold]
   502	    #[must_use]
   503	    pub fn concat(self, fix: CompositeFix) -> Self {
   504	        match (self, fix) {
   505	            (Self::None, f) | (f, Self::None) => f,
   506	            (Self::Single(fix1), Self::Single(fix2)) => Self::Multiple(vec![fix1, fix2]),
   507	            (Self::Single(fix), Self::Multiple(mut fixes)) => {
   508	                fixes.insert(0, fix);
   509	                Self::Multiple(fixes)
   510	            }
   511	            (Self::Multiple(mut fixes), Self::Single(fix)) => {
   512	                fixes.push(fix);
   513	                Self::Multiple(fixes)
   514	            }
   515	            (Self::Multiple(mut fixes1), Self::Multiple(fixes2)) => {
   516	                fixes1.extend(fixes2);
   517	                Self::Multiple(fixes1)
   518	            }
   519	        }
   520	    }
   521	
   522	    /// Gets the number of [`Fix`]es contained in this [`CompositeFix`].
   523	    pub fn len(&self) -> usize {
   524	        match self {
   525	            Self::None => 0,
   526	            Self::Single(_) => 1,
   527	            Self::Multiple(fs) => {
   528	                debug_assert!(
   529	                    fs.len() > 1,

    99	    /// State of newlines around a comment.
   100	    pub struct CommentNewlines: u8 {

   129	/// A comment in source code.
   130	#[ast]
   131	#[generate_derive(CloneIn, ContentEq, ESTree)]
   132	#[derive(Debug, Default, Clone, Copy, Eq, PartialEq)]
   133	#[estree(add_fields(value = CommentValue), no_ts_def, no_parent)]
   134	pub struct Comment {
   135	    /// The span of the comment text, with leading and trailing delimiters.
   136	    pub span: Span,
   137	
   138	    /// Start of token this leading comment is attached to.
   139	    /// `/* Leading */ token`
   140	    ///                ^ This start
   141	    /// NOTE: Trailing comment attachment is not computed yet.
   142	    #[estree(skip)]
   143	    pub attached_to: u32,
   144	
   145	    /// Line or block comment
   146	    #[estree(rename = "type")]
   147	    pub kind: CommentKind,
   148	
   149	    /// Leading or trailing comment
   150	    #[estree(skip)]
   151	    pub position: CommentPosition,
   152	
   153	    /// Whether this comment has newlines around it.
   154	    /// Used to avoid becoming a trailing comment in codegen.
   155	    #[estree(skip)]
   156	    pub newlines: CommentNewlines,
   157	
   158	    /// Content of the comment
   159	    #[estree(skip)]
   160	    pub content: CommentContent,
   161	}
   162	
   163	impl Comment {
   164	    /// Create a line or block comment at a given location.
   165	    #[inline]
   166	    pub fn new(start: u32, end: u32, kind: CommentKind) -> Self {
   167	        let span = Span::new(start, end);
   168	        Self {
   169	            span,
   170	            attached_to: 0,
   171	            kind,
   172	            position: CommentPosition::Trailing,
   173	            newlines: CommentNewlines::None,
   174	            content: CommentContent::None,
   175	        }
   176	    }
   177	
   178	    /// Gets the span of the comment content.
   179	    pub fn content_span(&self) -> Span {
   180	        match self.kind {
   181	            CommentKind::Line => Span::new(self.span.start + 2, self.span.end),
   182	            CommentKind::SingleLineBlock | CommentKind::MultiLineBlock => {
   183	                Span::new(self.span.start + 2, self.span.end - 2)
   184	            }
   185	        }
   186	    }
   187	
   188	    /// Returns `true` if this is a line comment.
   189	    #[inline]
   190	    pub fn is_line(self) -> bool {
   191	        self.kind == CommentKind::Line
   192	    }
   193	
   194	    /// Returns `true` if this is a block comment (either single-line or multi-line).
   195	    #[inline]
   196	    pub fn is_block(self) -> bool {
   197	        matches!(self.kind, CommentKind::SingleLineBlock | CommentKind::MultiLineBlock)
   198	    }
   199	
   200	    /// Returns `true` if this is a multi-line block comment.
   201	    #[inline]
   202	    pub fn is_multiline_block(self) -> bool {
   203	        self.kind == CommentKind::MultiLineBlock
   204	    }
   205	
   206	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is before a token.
   207	    #[inline]
   208	    pub fn is_leading(self) -> bool {
   209	        self.position == CommentPosition::Leading
   210	    }
   211	
   212	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is after a token.
   213	    #[inline]
   214	    pub fn is_trailing(self) -> bool {
   215	        self.position == CommentPosition::Trailing
   216	    }
   217	
   218	    /// Is comment without a special meaning.
   219	    #[inline]
   220	    pub fn is_normal(self) -> bool {
   221	        self.content == CommentContent::None
   222	    }
   223	
   224	    /// Is comment with special meaning.
   225	    #[inline]
   226	    pub fn is_annotation(self) -> bool {
   227	        self.content != CommentContent::None
   228	            && self.content != CommentContent::Legal
   229	            && self.content != CommentContent::Jsdoc
   230	            && self.content != CommentContent::JsdocLegal
   231	    }
   232	
   233	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is a JSDoc comment. Implies `is_leading` and `is_block`.
   234	    #[inline]
   235	    pub fn is_jsdoc(self) -> bool {
   236	        matches!(self.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc | CommentContent::JsdocLegal)
   237	            && self.is_leading()
   238	    }
   239	
   240	    /// Legal comments
   241	    ///
   242	    /// A "legal comment" is considered to be any statement-level comment
   243	    /// that contains `@license` or `@preserve` or that starts with `//!` or `/*!`.
   244	    ///
   245	    /// <https://esbuild.github.io/api/#legal-comments>
   246	    #[inline]
   247	    pub fn is_legal(self) -> bool {
   248	        matches!(self.content, CommentContent::Legal | CommentContent::JsdocLegal)
   249	            && self.is_leading()
   250	    }
   251	
   252	    /// Is `/* @__PURE__*/`.
   253	    #[inline]
   254	    pub fn is_pure(self) -> bool {
   255	        self.content == CommentContent::Pure
   256	    }
   257	
   258	    /// Is `/* @__NO_SIDE_EFFECTS__*/`.
   259	    #[inline]
   260	    pub fn is_no_side_effects(self) -> bool {
   261	        self.content == CommentContent::NoSideEffects
   262	    }
   263	
   264	    /// Is webpack magic comment.
   265	    #[inline]
   266	    pub fn is_webpack(self) -> bool {
   267	        self.content == CommentContent::Webpack
   268	    }
   269	
   270	    /// Is vite special comment.
   271	    #[inline]
   272	    pub fn is_vite(self) -> bool {
   273	        self.content == CommentContent::Vite
   274	    }
   275	
   276	    /// Is coverage ignore comment.
   277	    #[inline]
   278	    pub fn is_coverage_ignore(self) -> bool {
   279	        self.content == CommentContent::CoverageIgnore && self.is_leading()
   280	    }
   281	
   282	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is preceded by a newline.
   283	    #[inline]
   284	    pub fn preceded_by_newline(self) -> bool {
   285	        self.newlines.contains(CommentNewlines::Leading)
   286	    }
   287	
   288	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is followed by a newline.
   289	    #[inline]
   290	    pub fn followed_by_newline(self) -> bool {
   291	        self.newlines.contains(CommentNewlines::Trailing)
   292	    }
   293	
   294	    /// Returns `true` if this comment has newlines either before or after it.
   295	    #[inline]
   296	    pub fn has_newlines_around(self) -> bool {
   297	        self.newlines != CommentNewlines::None
   298	    }
   299	
   300	    /// Sets the state of `newlines` to include/exclude a newline before the comment.
   301	    #[inline]
   302	    pub fn set_preceded_by_newline(&mut self, preceded_by_newline: bool) {
   303	        self.newlines.set(CommentNewlines::Leading, preceded_by_newline);

Now I can see the key issue. `content_span()` returns:
- For line comments (`//`): `Span::new(self.span.start + 2, self.span.end)` — this skips the `//` prefix
- For block comments (`/* */`): `Span::new(self.span.start + 2, self.span.end - 2)` — this skips both `/*` and `*/`

So the `comment_span` used in the disable directives code (line 364) is the content span, which doesn't include the comment delimiters.

Now, when the fix is created in `create_unused_directives_report`:
- For `RuleCommentType::All`, line 284: `Fix::delete(span)` where `span` is this content span. This would delete only the content (e.g., `eslint-disable`) but leave the `//` or `/* */` delimiters, resulting in empty comments like `//` or `/**/`.

The fix should instead delete the entire comment span (including delimiters), i.e., `comment.span` rather than `comment.content_span()`.

   378	                    self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   379	                        span: comment_span,
   380	                        r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   381	                    });
   382	                    continue;
   383	                }
   384	                // `eslint-disable-next-line`
   385	                else if let Some(text) = text.strip_prefix("-next-line") {

   399	                    }
   400

   435	                    continue;
   436	                }
   437	                // `eslint-disable-line`
   438	                else if let Some(text) = text.strip_prefix("-line") {
   439	                    rule_name_start += 5; // -line is 5 bytes

```rust
pub fn comment_span(&self) -> &Span {
    match self {
        DisabledRule::All { comment_span, .. } | DisabledRule::Single { comment_span, .. } => {
            comment_span

    }

```

And the `comment_span` field is set in the builder from `comment.content_span()` (line 364). So yes, the span stored is the content span without `//` or `/* */`.

Now, the fix is in `create_unused_directives_report` in error_with_position.rs. The issue is that when we delete the span, we need to delete the full comment, not just the content.

But there's a complication: the `DisableRuleComment` only stores the content span, not the full comment span. We need to figure out the full span from the content span.

For line comments: content span starts at `full_span.start + 2`, so full span = `Span::new(content_span.start - 2, content_span.end)`.
For block comments: content span starts at `full_span.start + 2` and ends at `full_span.end - 2`, so full span = `Span::new(content_span.start - 2, content_span.end + 2)`.

But we don't know if it's a line or block comment from the span alone. We could look at the source text to determine this.

However, there's a simpler approach: we could modify the `DisableRuleComment` to also store the full comment span. Let me look at how it's used:

There are two approaches:

1. **Change `DisableRuleComment` to also store the full comment span** (the `comment.span` including delimiters). This would require changes in multiple places.

2. **In the fix creation code, expand the content span to include the comment delimiters.** We can determine whether it's a line comment (`//`) or block comment (`/* */`) by looking at the source text around the span.

Let me go with approach 2 since it's more localized. But actually, looking more carefully, we need to also consider that when we delete the entire comment line, we might also want to delete the newline after it to avoid leaving a blank line. Let me check what ESLint does.

Actually, let me re-read the PR description: "it strips the directive text and leaves an **empty comment** on the line (`//` or `/**/`) instead of **removing the whole line**"

So the expected behavior is to remove the whole line when nothing meaningful remains. That means we should:
1. Delete the entire comment (including `//` or `/* */`)
2. Also delete the newline after the comment (to avoid leaving a blank line)


2. Delete that

Now I can see the issue clearly. Look at the first code action for the "Fix All":

```
TextEdit: TextEdit {
    range: Range {
        start: Position {
            line: 0,
            character: 2,   <-- starts at character 2, after "//"
        },
        end: Position {
            line: 0,
            character: 56,
        },
    },
    new_text: "",
}
```

The range starts at character 2 (after `//`) and ends at character 56 (end of content). So it only deletes the content ` oxlint-disable-next-line no-debugger -- on wrong line` but leaves `//` behind. Same for line 8: starts at character 2, deletes content but leaves `//`.

The fix should start at character 0 (including `//`) and go to the end of the line (or at least the end of the comment). 

Now let me look at how this is generated. The issue is in `create_unused_directives_report`:

For `RuleCommentType::All`, the span is `unused_comment.span` which is the content span (without `//`). We need to expand this to include the full comment.

Let me also check the `RuleCommentType::Single` case. The `rule.create_fix` method uses `comment_span` which is also the content span, but it uses `self.name_span` for the rule name. That's fine for removing individual rules from a multi-rule disable comment.

The main fix should be in `create_unused_directives_report` in `error_with_position.rs`. But we also need to consider the CLI path. Let me check how the CLI handles this

   350	    #[expect(clippy::cast_possible_truncation)] // for `as u32`
   351	    fn build_impl(&mut self, source_text: &str, comments: &[Comment]) {
   352	        let source_len = source_text.len() as u32;
   353	        // This algorithm iterates through the comments and builds all intervals
   354	        // for matching disable and enable pairs.
   355	        // Wrongly ordered matching pairs are not taken into consideration.
   356	
   357	        // NOTE: oxlint apply directive's logic not exactly same to eslint
   358	        // only `disable-all` & `enable-all`, or `disable-rule` & `enable-rule` will add to intervals for disable directives
   359	        // `disable-all` & `enable-rule` -> lone `disable-all` (enable-rule find not disable-rule before itself)
   360	        // https://github.com/eslint/eslint/blob/f67d5e875324a9d899598b11807a9c7624021432/lib/linter/apply-disable-directives.js#L308
   361	
   362	        // enable directive keep the same logic for checking unused
   363	        let mut unused_enable_directives: Vec<(Option<String>, Span)> = vec![];
   364	
   365	        for comment in comments {
   366	            let comment_span = comment.content_span();
   367	            let text_source = comment_span.source_text(source_text);
   368	            let text = text_source.trim_start();
   369	            let mut rule_name_start = comment_span.start + (text_source.len() - text.len()) as u32;
   370	
   371	            if let Some(text) =
   372	                text.strip_prefix("eslint-disable").or_else(|| text.strip_prefix("oxlint-disable"))
   373	            {
   374	                rule_name_start += 14; // eslint-disable and oxlint-disable are each 14 bytes
   375	                // `eslint-disable`
   376	                if text.trim().is_empty() {
   377	                    if self.disable_all_start.is_none() {
   378	                        self.disable_all_start = Some((comment_span.end, comment_span));
   379	                    }
   380	                    self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   381	                        span: comment_span,
   382	                        r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   383	                    });
   384	                    continue;
   385	                }
   386	                // `eslint-disable-next-line`
   387	                else if let Some(text) = text.strip_prefix("-next-line") {
   388	                    rule_name_start += 10; // -next-line is 10 bytes
   389	                    // Get the span up to the next new line
   390	                    let mut stop = comment_span.end;
   391	                    let mut lines_after_comment_end =
   392	                        source_text[comment_span.end as usize..].split_inclusive('\n');
   393	
   394	                    if let Some(rest_of_line) = lines_after_comment_end.next() {
   395	                        stop += rest_of_line.len() as u32;
   396	                    }
   397	
   398	                    if let Some(next_line) = lines_after_comment_end.next() {
   399	                        let next_line_trimmed = next_line.trim_end_matches(['\n', '\r']);
   400	                        stop += next_line_trimmed.len() as u32;
   401	                    }
   402	
   403	                    if text.trim().is_empty() {
   404	                        self.add_interval(
   405	                            comment_span.end,
   406	                            stop,
   407	                            DisabledRule::All { comment_span, is_next_line: true },
   408	                        );
   409	                        self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   410	                            span: comment_span,
   411	                            r#type: RuleCommentType::All,
   412	                        });
   413	                    } else {
   414	                        // `eslint-disable-next-line rule_name1, rule_name2`
   415	                        let mut rules = vec![];
   416	                        Self::get_rule_names(text, rule_name_start, |rule_name, name_span| {
   417	                            self.add_interval(
   418	                                comment_span.end,
   419	                                stop,
   420	                                DisabledRule::Single {
   421	                                    rule_name: rule_name.to_string(),
   422	                                    name_span,
   423	                                    comment_span,
   424	                                    is_next_line: true,
   425	                                },
   426	                            );
   427	                            rules.push(RuleCommentRule {
   428	                                rule_name: rule_name.to_string(),
   429	                                name_span,
   430	                            });
   431	                        });
   432	                        self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   433	                            span: comment_span,
   434	                            r#type: RuleCommentType::Single(rules),
   435	                        });
   436	                    }
   437	                    continue;
   438	                }
   439	                // `eslint-disable-line`
   440	                else if let Some(text) = text.strip_prefix("-line") {
   441	                    rule_name_start += 5; // -line is 5 bytes
   442	
   443	                    // Get the span between the preceding newline to this comment
   444	                    let start = source_text[..comment_span.start as usize]
   445	                        .lines()
   446	                        .next_back()
   447	                        .map_or(0, |line| comment_span.start - line.len() as u32);
   448	                    let stop = comment_span.start;
   449

   451	                    if text.trim().is_empty() {

   482	                            r#type: RuleCommentType::Single(rules),
   483	                        });
   484	                    }
   485	                    continue;
   486	                }
   487	                // Remaining text should start with a whitespace character, else it's probably a typo of the correct syntax.
   488	                // Like `eslint-disable-lext-nine` where `text` is `-lext-nine`, or directive is `eslint-disablefoo`
   489	                else if text.starts_with(char::is_whitespace) {
   490	                    // `eslint-disable rule-name1, rule-name2`
   491	                    let mut rules = vec![];
   492	                    Self::get_rule_names(text, rule_name_start, |rule_name, name_span| {
   493	                        self.disable_start_map.entry(rule_name.to_string()).or_insert((
   494	                            comment_span.end,
   495	                            name_span,
   496	                            comment_span,
   497	                        ));
   498	                        rules.push(RuleCommentRule { rule_name: rule_name.to_string(), name_span });
   499	                    });
   500	                    self.disable_rule_comments.push(DisableRuleComment {
   501	                        span: comment_span,
   502	                        r#type: RuleCommentType::Single(rules),
   503	                    });
   504	                    continue;
   505	                }
